Title: List of Nvidia graphics processing units - Wikipedia
[Jump to content](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#bodyContent)

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

This list contains general information about [graphics processing units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit "Graphics processing unit") (GPUs) and [video cards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_card "Video card") from [Nvidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia "Nvidia"), based on official specifications. In addition some [Nvidia motherboards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_of_Nvidia_nForce_chipsets "Comparison of Nvidia nForce chipsets") come with integrated onboard GPUs. Limited/special/collectors' editions or AIB versions are not included.

## Field explanations

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Field explanations")\]

The fields in the table listed below describe the following:

- _Model_ – The marketing name for the processor, assigned by Nvidia.
- _Launch_ – Date of release for the processor.
- _Code name_ – The internal engineering codename for the processor (typically designated by an NVXY name and later GXY where X is the series number and Y is the schedule of the project for that generation).
- _[Fab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor_device_fabrication "Semiconductor device fabrication")_ – Fabrication process. Average feature size of components of the processor.
- _[Bus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bus_(computing) "Bus (computing)") interface_ – Bus by which the graphics processor is attached to the system (typically an expansion slot, such as PCI, AGP, or PCI-Express).
- _[Memory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random-access_memory "Random-access memory")_ – The amount of graphics memory available to the processor.
- _SM Count_ – Number of streaming multiprocessors.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-SMCount-motherboardsdotorg-1)
- _Core [clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clock_rate "Clock rate")_ – The factory core clock frequency; while some manufacturers adjust clocks lower and higher, this number will always be the reference clocks used by Nvidia.
- _Memory clock_ – The factory effective memory clock frequency (while some manufacturers adjust clocks lower and higher, this number will always be the reference clocks used by Nvidia). All DDR/GDDR memories operate at half this frequency, except for GDDR5, which operates at one quarter of this frequency.
- _Core config_ – The layout of the graphics pipeline, in terms of functional units. Over time the number, type, and variety of functional units in the GPU core has changed significantly; before each section in the list there is an explanation as to what functional units are present in each generation of processors. In later models, shaders are integrated into a unified shader architecture, where any one shader can perform any of the functions listed.
- _[Fillrate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fillrate "Fillrate")_ – Maximum theoretical fill rate in textured pixels per second. This number is generally used as a _maximum throughput number_ for the GPU and generally, a higher fill rate corresponds to a more powerful (and faster) GPU.
- _Memory subsection_
  - _[Bandwidth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing) "Bandwidth (computing)")_ – Maximum theoretical bandwidth for the processor at factory clock with factory bus width. GHz = 109 Hz.
  - _Bus type_ – Type of memory bus or buses used.
  - _Bus width_ – Maximum bit width of the memory bus or buses used. This will always be a factory bus width.
- _API support section_
  - _[Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D")_ – Maximum version of Direct3D fully supported.
  - _[OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL")_ – Maximum version of OpenGL fully supported.
  - [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") – Maximum version of OpenCL fully supported.
  - [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") – Maximum version of Vulkan fully supported.
  - [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") \- Maximum version of Cuda fully supported.
- _Features_ – Added features that are not standard as a part of the two graphics libraries.

2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-8 "Jump up")**Only 16MB versions of the Vanta LT were found with AGP 4x interfaces.
3. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-9 "Jump up")**PCI was much rarer on the Riva TNT2 Pro / Ultra cards compared to AGP 4x.
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-10 "Jump up")**Some cards ran at 143MHz and only had 1.14GB/s bandwidth, but almost all were 150MHZ.

### GeForce 256 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: GeForce 256 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 256](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_256 "GeForce 256") and [Celsius (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celsius_(microarchitecture) "Celsius (microarchitecture)")

- All models are made via [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") [220 nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/250_nm_process "250 nm process") fabrication process
- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 7.0 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 1.2
- All models support hardware Transform and Lighting (T&L) and Cube Environment Mapping

### GeForce2 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: GeForce2 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 2 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_2_series "GeForce 2 series") and [Celsius (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celsius_(microarchitecture) "Celsius (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 7 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 1.2
- All models support TwinView Dual-Display Architecture, Second-Generation Transform and Lighting (T&L),

Nvidia Shading Rasterizer (NSR), High-Definition Video Processor (HDVP)
- GeForce2 MX models support Digital Vibrance Control (DVC)

### GeForce3 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: GeForce3 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 3 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_3_series "GeForce 3 series") and [Kelvin (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelvin_(microarchitecture) "Kelvin (microarchitecture)")

- All models are made via [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") [150 nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/180_nm_process "180 nm process") fabrication process
- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 8.0 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 1.3
- All models support 3D Textures, Lightspeed Memory Architecture (LMA), nFiniteFX Engine, Shadow Buffers

### GeForce4 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: GeForce4 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 4 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_4_series "GeForce 4 series") and [Kelvin (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelvin_(microarchitecture) "Kelvin (microarchitecture)")

- All models are manufactured via [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") [150 nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/180_nm_process "180 nm process") manufacturing process
- All models support Accuview Antialiasing (AA), Lightspeed Memory Architecture II (LMA II), nView

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-geforce_4_2_23-0 "Jump up")**GeForce4 Ti4400 8x: Card manufacturers utilizing this chip labeled the card as a Ti4800SE. The surface of the chip has "Ti-8x" printed on it.
2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-geforce_4_3_24-0 "Jump up")**GeForce4 Ti4600 8x: Card manufacturers utilizing this chip labeled the card as a Ti4600, and in some cases as a Ti4800. The surface of the chip has "Ti-8x" printed on it, as well as "4800" printed at the bottom.

### GeForce FX (5xxx) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: GeForce FX (5xxx) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce FX series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_FX_series "GeForce FX series") and [Rankine (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rankine_(microarchitecture) "Rankine (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 9.0a and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 1.5 (2.1 (software) with latest drivers)
- The GeForce FX series runs vertex shaders in an array

### GeForce 6 (6xxx) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: GeForce 6 (6xxx) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 6 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_6_series "GeForce 6 series") and [Curie (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curie_(microarchitecture) "Curie (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 9.0c and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 2.1
- All models support Transparency [AA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spatial_anti-aliasing "Spatial anti-aliasing") (starting with version 91.47 of the ForceWare drivers) and PureVideo

### GeForce 7 (7xxx) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: GeForce 7 (7xxx) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 7 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_7_series "GeForce 7 series") and [Curie (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curie_(microarchitecture) "Curie (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 9.0c and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 2.1
- All models except the 7025, 7050PV, 7050, 7100, 7150, & 7100 GS support gamma-correct [antialiasing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antialiasing "Antialiasing") & 64-bit OpenEXR HDR.
- All models support Transparency [AA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spatial_anti-aliasing "Spatial anti-aliasing") (starting with version 91.47 of the ForceWare drivers)

### GeForce 8 (8xxx) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: GeForce 8 (8xxx) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 8 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_8_series "GeForce 8 series") and [Tesla (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(microarchitecture) "Tesla (microarchitecture)")

- All models support coverage sample anti-aliasing, angle-independent anisotropic filtering, and 128-bit OpenEXR HDR.
- All models with [PureVideo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PureVideo "PureVideo") 2 & 3 support the BSP Engine & AES128 Engine.
- Compute Capability 1.1: has support for Atomic functions, which are used to write thread-safe programs.
- Compute Capability 1.2: for details see [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA#Version_features_and_specifications "CUDA")

### GeForce 9 (9xxx) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: GeForce 9 (9xxx) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 9 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_9_series "GeForce 9 series") and [Tesla (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(microarchitecture) "Tesla (microarchitecture)")

- All models support Coverage Sample Anti-Aliasing, Angle-Independent Anisotropic Filtering, 128-bit OpenEXR HDR
- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 10.0 & [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 3.3.
- Compute Capability: 1.1 has support for Atomic functions, which are used to write thread-safe programs.
- All models support 2-Way [SLI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scalable_Link_Interface "Scalable Link Interface") except for the 9800 GTX & 9800 GTX+ which support 3-Way, and the integrated models do not support it at all.
- All models support [PureVideo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PureVideo "PureVideo") 2 with the VP2, BSP Engine, and AES128 Engine, except for models that use the G98 core, which instead support [PureVideo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PureVideo "PureVideo") 3 with the VP3, BSP Engine, and AES128 Engine.

### GeForce 200 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: GeForce 200 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 200 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_200_series "GeForce 200 series") and [Tesla (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(microarchitecture) "Tesla (microarchitecture)")

- All models support Coverage Sample Anti-Aliasing, Angle-Independent Anisotropic Filtering, 240-bit OpenEXR HDR.
- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 10.0 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 3.3, except the GeForce 205, 210, 220, & GT 240, which support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 10.1 instead.
- Compute Capability: 1.1 (G92 \[GTS250\] GPU).
- Compute Capability: 1.2 (GT215, GT216, GT218 GPUs).
- Compute Capability: 1.3 has [double precision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double-precision_floating-point_format "Double-precision floating-point format") support for use in [GPGPU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GPGPU "GPGPU") applications. (GT200a/b GPUs only).

### GeForce 300 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: GeForce 300 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 300 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_300_series "GeForce 300 series") and [Tesla (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(microarchitecture) "Tesla (microarchitecture)")

- All models support the following [API](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface") levels: [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 10.1 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 3.3
- None of the models needs an external power source.
- All models are OEM only cards.

### GeForce 400 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: GeForce 400 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 400 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_400_series "GeForce 400 series") and [Fermi (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture) "Fermi (microarchitecture)")

- All cards have a PCIe 2.0 x16 [Bus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_bus "Computer bus") [interface](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I/O_interface "I/O interface").
- All models support [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.0, [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (11\_0), & [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 2.1 except the GeForce 405, which has no [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan")[\[a\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-85) support, supports [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 3.3, [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 11.1 (10\_1), & [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 1.2 instead, and the GF-100 Core, which supports [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 2.0 instead.
- All models support [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 1.1.
- All models are built on the 40 [nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanometer "Nanometer") process at the [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") [Fab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor_device_fabrication "Semiconductor device fabrication").

### GeForce 500 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: GeForce 500 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 500 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_500_series "GeForce 500 series") and [Fermi (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture) "Fermi (microarchitecture)")

- All models lack [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") support but support, [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (11\_0), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 1.1, & [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 2.1, except for the GTX 570, GTX 580, & GTX 590, which supports [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 2.0 instead.
- All models are built on the 40 [nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanometer "Nanometer") process at the [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") [Fab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor_device_fabrication "Semiconductor device fabrication").

### GeForce 600 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: GeForce 600 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 600 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_600_series "GeForce 600 series") and [Kepler (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler_(microarchitecture) "Kepler (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (11\_0), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, & [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 1.2.
- Only Kepler (28 nm) models support [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.2.
- All Kepler (28 nm) models function at 2 [FLOPS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FLOPS "FLOPS") per clock per core compared to only 1 [FLOP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FLOP "FLOP") per clock per core on Fermi (40 nm) models. This however only applies to single precision.
- Texel and Pixel rate calculated by multiplying clock in MHz to their respective cores.
- Many models are rebranded 400 or 500 series GPUs.

### GeForce 700 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: GeForce 700 series")\]

- All GM107-chips are [Maxwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell_(microarchitecture) "Maxwell (microarchitecture)")-based, all GF1xx are [Fermi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture) "Fermi (microarchitecture)")-based, and all GKxxx-chips are [Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler_(microarchitecture) "Kepler (microarchitecture)")-based.
- Many models are rebranded cards from previous generations.
- API Support:
  - All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (11\_0). [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6.
  - [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan"): Maxwell chips support 1.3, Kepler chips support 1.2, & Fermi lacks support.
  - [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL"): Maxwell and Kepler chips support 3.0, while Fermi chips only support 1.1.
- GTX TITAN class cards use Double precision 1:3 instead of 1:24 or 1:32 found on other GTX 700 series cards.

### GeForce 900 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: GeForce 900 series")\]

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_1), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, and [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.4.
- All models are built on the [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") 28 [nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanometer "Nanometer") process and interface with a PCIe 3x16 connector.

### GeForce 10 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: GeForce 10 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 10 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_10_series "GeForce 10 series") and [Pascal (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(microarchitecture) "Pascal (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_1), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.4, and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 6.1.

### Volta series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Volta series")\]

Further information: [Volta (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volta_(microarchitecture) "Volta (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_1), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.4, and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 7.0.
- All models are built on the [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") 12 nm process with 21.1 billion transistors and a die size of 815 mm2.

### GeForce RTX 20 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 20 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 20 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_20_series "GeForce RTX 20 series") and [Turing (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_(microarchitecture) "Turing (microarchitecture)")

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 Ultimate (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3, and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 7.5.
- Founder's Edition variants come from the factory with a higher boost clock.
- All models are built on the [TSMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSMC "TSMC") 12 nm process and interface with a PCIe 3x16 connector.

### GeForce RTX 30 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 30 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 30 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_30_series "GeForce RTX 30 series") and [Ampere (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ampere_(microarchitecture) "Ampere (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 Ultimate (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3[\[223\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-vulkandrv-247) and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 8.6
- Supported display connections: [HDMI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HDMI "HDMI") 2.1, [DisplayPort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DisplayPort "DisplayPort") 1.4a
- [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC") 7th generation
- [Tensor core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_Core "Tensor Core") 3rd gen
- [RT Core](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=RT_Core&action=edit&redlink=1 "RT Core (page does not exist)") 2nd gen
- RTX IO
- Improved [NVDEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia_NVDEC "Nvidia NVDEC") with [AV1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AV1 "AV1") decode
- NVIDIA [DLSS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DLSS "DLSS") 2.0

### GeForce RTX 40 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 40 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 40 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_40_series "GeForce RTX 40 series") and [Ada Lovelace (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ada_Lovelace_(microarchitecture) "Ada Lovelace (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 Ultimate (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3 and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 8.9[\[240\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-265)
- Supported display connections: [HDMI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HDMI "HDMI") 2.1, [DisplayPort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DisplayPort "DisplayPort") 1.4a
- [Tensor core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_Core "Tensor Core") 4th gen
- [RT core](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=RT_core&action=edit&redlink=1 "RT core (page does not exist)") 3rd gen
- NVIDIA [DLSS 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DLSS "DLSS")
- NVIDIA [DLSS 3.5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DLSS "DLSS")
- [Shader Execution Reordering](https://developer.nvidia.com/blog/improve-shader-performance-and-in-game-frame-rates-with-shader-execution-reordering/)
- Dual [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC") with 8K 10-bit 60FPS [AV1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AV1 "AV1") fixed function hardware encoding[\[241\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-266)[\[242\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-267)
- Opacity Micro-Maps (OMM)
- Displacement Micro-Meshes (DMM)
- No NVLink support, Multi-GPU over PCIe 5.0[\[243\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-268)[\[244\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-269)

### GeForce RTX 50 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 50 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 50 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_50_series "GeForce RTX 50 series") and [Blackwell (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackwell_(microarchitecture) "Blackwell (microarchitecture)")

- GeForce RTX 50 series desktop GPUs are the first consumer GPUs to utilize a [PCIe 5.0](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PCI_Express#PCI_Express_5.0 "PCI Express") interface and [GDDR7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDDR7_SDRAM "GDDR7 SDRAM") video memory.
- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12.2, [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.4 and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 12.x
- Supported display connections: [HDMI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HDMI "HDMI") 2.1b, [DisplayPort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DisplayPort "DisplayPort") 2.1b
- 9th gen [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC") (3×/2×/1×) / 6th gen [NVDEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVDEC "NVDEC") (2×/1×)
- NVIDIA [DLSS 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_Learning_Super_Sampling "Deep Learning Super Sampling") (Multi Frame Generation support)
- AI Management Processor ( [AMP](https://www.techpowerup.com/review/nvidia-geforce-rtx-50-technical-deep-dive/3.html#:~:text=address%20this%2C%20the-,AI%20Management%20Processor%20(AMP),-was%20introduced%20as))
- [Reflex](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/geforce/news/reflex-2-even-lower-latency-gameplay-with-frame-warp/) 2 optimized
- [Tensor core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_core "Tensor core") 5th gen (INT4/FP4 capabilities and second-generation FP8 Transformer Engine)
- [RT core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray-tracing_hardware "Ray-tracing hardware") 4th gen
- [Shader processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"), [RT cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_hardware "Ray tracing hardware") and [tensor cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_core "Tensor core") optimized for RTX [Neural Shaders](https://developer.nvidia.com/blog/nvidia-rtx-neural-rendering-introduces-next-era-of-ai-powered-graphics-innovation/) and new neural workloads
- [Mega Geometry](https://github.com/NVIDIA-RTX/RTXMG) Technology optimized (Shader processors and RT cores)
- [Shader Execution Reordering](https://developer.nvidia.com/blog/improve-shader-performance-and-in-game-frame-rates-with-shader-execution-reordering/) (SER) 2.0
- [Linear Swept Spheres](https://developer.nvidia.com/blog/render-path-traced-hair-in-real-time-with-nvidia-geforce-rtx-50-series-gpus/) (LSS)

## Mobile GPUs

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Mobile GPUs")\]

Mobile GPUs are either soldered to the mainboard or to some [Mobile PCI Express Module](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobile_PCI_Express_Module "Mobile PCI Express Module") (MXM).

- All models support [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 7.0 and [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 1.2

### GeForce 400M (4xxM) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: GeForce 400M (4xxM) series")\]

The GeForce 400M series for notebooks architecture, [Fermi (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture) "Fermi (microarchitecture)")

- 1 [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- 2 To calculate the processing power see [Fermi (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Fermi (microarchitecture)").
- 3 Each SM in the GF100 also contains 4 texture address units and 16 texture filtering units. Total for the full GF100 64 texture address units and 256 texture filtering units.[\[266\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-anandtech.com-295) Each SM in the GF104/106/108 architecture contains 8 texture filtering units for every texture address unit. The complete GF104 die contains 64 texture address units and 512 texture filtering units, the complete GF106 die contains 32 texture address units and 256 texture filtering units and the complete GF108 die contains 16 texture address units and 128 texture filtering units.

### GeForce 600M (6xxM) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: GeForce 600M (6xxM) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 600 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_600_series "GeForce 600 series")

The GeForce 600M series for notebooks architecture, [Fermi (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture) "Fermi (microarchitecture)") and [Kepler (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler_(microarchitecture) "Kepler (microarchitecture)"). The processing power is obtained by multiplying shader clock speed, the number of cores, and how many instructions the cores can perform per cycle.

- 1 [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- Non GTX Graphics, lack support [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC")

### GeForce 800M (8xxM) series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: GeForce 800M (8xxM) series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 800M series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_800M_series "GeForce 800M series")

The GeForce 800M series for notebooks architecture. The processing power is obtained by multiplying shader clock speed, the number of cores, and how many instructions the cores can perform per cycle.

- 1 [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- 810M to 845M lack [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC") support

### GeForce 10 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: GeForce 10 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 10 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_10_series "GeForce 10 series") and [Pascal (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(microarchitecture) "Pascal (microarchitecture)")

- [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- Improved NVENC (Better support for H265, VP9,...)
- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_1), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3 and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 6.1[\[280\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-cuda-gpu-cap-309)

### GeForce 16 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: GeForce 16 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce 16 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_16_series "GeForce 16 series") and [Turing (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_(microarchitecture) "Turing (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_1), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3 and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 7.5, improve [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia_NVENC "Nvidia NVENC")
- No [SLI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scalable_Link_Interface "Scalable Link Interface"), no TensorCore, and no [Raytracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics) "Ray tracing (graphics)") hardware acceleration.

### GeForce RTX 20 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 20 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 20 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_20_series "GeForce RTX 20 series") and [Turing (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_(microarchitecture) "Turing (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3 and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 7.5, improve [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia_NVENC "Nvidia NVENC") (Support B-Frame on [H265](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Efficiency_Video_Coding "High Efficiency Video Coding")...)
- MX Graphics lack [NVENC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NVENC "NVENC") and they are based on Pascal architecture.[\[316\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-345)
- Add TensorCore and [Ray tracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics) "Ray tracing (graphics)") hardware acceleration, RTX IO (Only on RTX cards)
- Nvidia DLSS

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-CoreConfig_346-0 "Jump up")**Main [Shader Processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model") **:** [Texture Mapping Units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit") **:** [Render Output Units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit") **:** [Tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor "Tensor") Cores (or FP16 Cores in GeForce 16 series) **:** [Ray-tracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics) "Ray tracing (graphics)") Cores (Streaming Multiprocessors) (Graphics Processing Clusters)
2. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_347-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_347-1)Base clock, Boost clock
3. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PixelFillrate_348-0 "Jump up")**Pixel fillrate is calculated as the lowest of three numbers: number of ROPs multiplied by the base core clock speed, number of rasterizers multiplied by the number of fragments they can generate per rasterizer multiplied by the base core clock speed, and the number of streaming multiprocessors multiplied by the number of fragments per clock that they can output multiplied by the base clock rate.
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-TextureFillrate_349-0 "Jump up")**Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of TMUs multiplied by the base core clock speed.

### GeForce RTX 30 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 30 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 30 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_30_series "GeForce RTX 30 series") and [Ampere (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ampere_(microarchitecture) "Ampere (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 Ultimate (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3[\[223\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-vulkandrv-247) and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 8.6
- [Tensor core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_Core "Tensor Core") 3rd gen
- [RT core](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=RT_core&action=edit&redlink=1 "RT core (page does not exist)") 2nd gen
- RTX IO
- Improve [NVDEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia_NVDEC "Nvidia NVDEC") (Add AV1)

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ClockSpeed_362-0 "Jump up")**Which base and boost core clockspeeds the GPU has depends on the TDP configuration set by the system builder
2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-CoreConfig_363-0 "Jump up")**Main [Shader Processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model") **:** [Texture Mapping Units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit") **:** [Render Output Units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit") **:** [Tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor "Tensor") Cores (or FP16 Cores in GeForce 16 series) **:** [Ray-tracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics) "Ray tracing (graphics)") Cores (Streaming Multiprocessors) (Graphics Processing Clusters)
3. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_364-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_364-1)Base clock, Boost clock.
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PixelFillrate_365-0 "Jump up")**Pixel fillrate is calculated as the lowest of three numbers: number of ROPs multiplied by the base core clock speed, number of rasterizers multiplied by the number of fragments they can generate per rasterizer multiplied by the base core clock speed, and the number of streaming multiprocessors multiplied by the number of fragments per clock that they can output multiplied by the base clock rate.
5. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-TextureFillrate_366-0 "Jump up")**Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of TMUs multiplied by the base core clock speed.

### GeForce RTX 40 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 40 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 40 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_40_series "GeForce RTX 40 series") and [Ada Lovelace (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ada_Lovelace_(microarchitecture) "Ada Lovelace (microarchitecture)")

- Supported [APIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface "Application programming interface"): [Direct3D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct3D "Direct3D") 12 Ultimate (12\_2), [OpenGL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL "OpenGL") 4.6, [OpenCL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL "OpenCL") 3.0, [Vulkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulkan "Vulkan") 1.3[\[223\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-vulkandrv-247) and [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") 8.9
- [Tensor core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_Core "Tensor Core") 4th gen
- [RT core](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=RT_core&action=edit&redlink=1 "RT core (page does not exist)") 3rd gen
- DLSS 3 (Super Resolution + Frame Generation)[\[342\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-380)
- SER[\[343\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-381)

### GeForce RTX 50 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: GeForce RTX 50 series")\]

Further information: [GeForce RTX 50 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_RTX_50_series "GeForce RTX 50 series") and [Blackwell (microarchitecture)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackwell_(microarchitecture) "Blackwell (microarchitecture)")

Laptops featuring GeForce RTX 50 series laptop GPUs were shown at CES 2025. Laptops with RTX 50 series GPUs were paired with [Intel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intel "Intel")'s [Arrow Lake-HX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow_Lake_(microprocessor) "Arrow Lake (microprocessor)") and [AMD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices "Advanced Micro Devices")'s Strix Point and Fire Range CPUs.[\[346\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-389)[\[347\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-390) Nvidia claims that Blackwell architecture's new Max-Q features can increase battery life by up to 40% over GeForce 40 series laptops.[\[348\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-391) For example, Advanced Power Gating saves power by turning off areas of the GPU that are unused and the paired GDDR7 memory can run in an "ultra" low-voltage state.[\[349\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-392) Initial RTX 50 series laptops will become available in March 2025.[\[350\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-393)

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-CoreConfig_405-0 "Jump up")**[Shader Processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model") : [Texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit") : [Render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit") : Streaming Multiprocessors : [Ray tracing cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia_RTX "Nvidia RTX") : [Tensor Cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_Core "Tensor Core")
2. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_406-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PerfValues_406-1)Base clock, Boost clock
3. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-PixelFillrate_407-0 "Jump up")**Pixel fillrate is calculated as the lowest of three numbers: number of ROPs multiplied by the base core clock speed, number of rasterizers multiplied by the number of fragments they can generate per rasterizer multiplied by the base core clock speed, and the number of streaming multiprocessors multiplied by the number of fragments per clock that they can output multiplied by the base clock rate.
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-TextureFillrate_408-0 "Jump up")**Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of TMUs multiplied by the base core clock speed.

### Quadro Go (GL) & Quadro FX Go series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Quadro Go (GL) & Quadro FX Go series")\]

Further information: [Quadro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadro "Quadro")

Early mobile Quadro chips based on the GeForce2 Go up to GeForce Go 6800. Precise specifications on these old mobile workstation chips are very hard to find, and conflicting between Nvidia press releases and product lineups in GPU databases like TechPowerUp's GPUDB.

- 1 [Vertex shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertex_shader "Vertex shader"): [pixel shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pixel_shader "Pixel shader"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- 2 [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")

### Quadro x000 series

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units&action=edit&section=65 "Edit section: Quadro x000 series")\]

Further information: [Quadro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadro "Quadro")

- 1 [Unified shaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model"): [texture mapping units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit"): [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit")
- 4 Each SM in the Fermi architecture contains 4 texture filtering units for every texture address unit. Total for the full GF100 64 texture address units and 256 texture filtering units[\[266\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-anandtech.com-295)

Notes

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Calculate_521-0 "Jump up")**To calculate the processing power see [Tesla (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Tesla (microarchitecture)"), [Fermi (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Fermi (microarchitecture)"), [Kepler (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Kepler (microarchitecture)"), [Maxwell (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Maxwell (microarchitecture)"), or [Pascal (microarchitecture)#Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(microarchitecture)#Performance "Pascal (microarchitecture)"). A number range specifies the minimum and maximum processing power at, respectively, the base clock and maximum boost clock.
2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-522 "Jump up")**Core architecture version according to the [CUDA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CUDA "CUDA") programming guide.
3. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-CoreConfig_523-0 "Jump up")**Main [shader processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_shader_model "Unified shader model") : [texture mapping unit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texture_mapping_unit "Texture mapping unit") : [render output units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Render_output_unit "Render output unit") : [tensor cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_core "Tensor core") : [ray-tracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics) "Ray tracing (graphics)") cores (streaming multiprocessors)
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-GPUBoost_525-0 "Jump up")**GPU Boost is a default feature that increases the core clock rate while remaining under the card's predetermined power budget. Multiple boost clocks are available, but this table lists the highest clock supported by each card.[\[472\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_note-524)
5. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed8800_526-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed8800_526-1) [_**c**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed8800_526-2)Specifications not specified by Nvidia assumed to be based on the [GeForce 8800](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_8800 "GeForce 8800") GTX
6. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed280_527-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed280_527-1) [_**c**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed280_527-2) [_**d**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed280_527-3)Specifications not specified by Nvidia assumed to be based on the [GeForce GTX 280](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_200_series#GeForce_GTX_200 "GeForce 200 series")
7. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed5800_530-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-Assumed5800_530-1)Specifications not specified by Nvidia assumed to be based on the Quadro FX 5800
8. ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-0) [_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-1) [_**c**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-2) [_**d**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-3) [_**e**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-4) [_**f**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nvidia_graphics_processing_units#cite_ref-ECC_532-5)With ECC on, a portion of the dedicated memory is used for ECC bits, so the available user memory is reduced by 12.5%. (e.g. 4 GB total memory yields 3.5 GB of user available memory.)

- A10G GPU accelerator (PCIe card)-300W TDP, Ampere, 24GB GDDR6@600GB/s, 80 RT Cores

Title: [PDF] The Evolution of GPUs for General Purpose Computing - NVIDIA
# The Evolution of GPUs for General Purpose Computing

Ian Buck\| Sr. Director GPU Computing Software

San Jose Convention Center, CA \| September 20–23, 2010

* * *

# Talk Outline

- History of early graphics hardware • First GPU Computing
- When GPUs became programmable • Creating GPU Computing
- Future Trends and directions

* * *

# First Generation-Wireframe

- Vertex: transform, clip, and project • Rasterization: lines only
- Pixel: no pixels! calligraphic display • Dates: prior to 1987

* * *

# Storage Tube Terminals

- CRTs with analog charge ―persistence‖ • Accumulate a detailed static image by writing points or

## line segments • Erase the stored image to start a new one

* * *

# Early Framebuffers

- By the mid-1970’s one could afford framebuffers with a few bits per pixel at modest resolution

### — ―A Random Access Video Frame Buffer‖, Kajiya, Sutherland, Cheadle, 1975

- Vector displays were still better for fine position detail • Framebuffers were used to emulate storage tube vector

## terminals on a raster display

* * *

# Second Generation – Shaded Solids

- Vertex: lighting • Rasterization: filled polygons
- Pixel: depth buffer, color blending • Dates: 1987 - 1992

* * *

# Third Generation – Texture Mapping

- Vertex: more, faster • Rasterization: more, faster
- Pixel: texture filtering, antialiasing • Dates: 1992 - 2001

* * *

# IRIS 3000 Graphics Cards

## 4 bit / pixel Framebuffer Geometry Engines & Rasterizer (2 instances)

* * *

# 1990’s

- Desktop 3D workstations under $5000 — Single-board, multi-chip graphics subsystems
- Rise of 3D on the PC — 40 company free-for-all until intense competition knocked out all but a few players — Many were ―decelerators‖, and easy to beat — Single-chip GPUs — Interesting hardware experimentation — PCs would take over the workstation business
- Interesting consoles — 3DO, Nintendo, Sega, Sony

* * *

# Before Programmable Shading

- Computing though image processing circa.1995

### — GL\_ARB\_imaging

* * *

# Programmable Shaders: GeForceFX (2002)

- Vertex and fragment operations specified in small (macro) assembly language
- User-specified mapping of input data to operations • Limited ability to use intermediate computed values to

## index input data (textures and vertex uniforms)

ADDR R0.xyz, eyePosition.xyzx, -f\[TEX0\].xyzx; DP3R R0.w, R0.xyzx, R0.xyzx; RSQR R0.w, R0.w; MULR R0.xyz, R0.w, R0.xyzx; ADDR R1.xyz, lightPosition.xyzx, -f\[TEX0\].xyzx; DP3R R0.w, R1.xyzx, R1.xyzx; RSQR R0.w, R0.w; MADR R0.xyz, R0.w, R1.xyzx, R0.xyzx; MULR R1.xyz, R0.w, R1.xyzx; DP3R R0.w, R1.xyzx, f\[TEX1\].xyzx; MAXR R0.w, R0.w, {0}.x;

# Early GPGPU (2002)

# Programming model challenge

- Demonstrate GPU performace • PHD computer graphics to do this
- Financial companies hiring game programmers
- ―GPU as a processor‖

* * *

# Brook (2003)

## C with streams • streams

### – collection of records requiring similar computation

- particle positions, voxels, FEM cell, … **Ray r<200>;** **float3 velocityfield<100,100,100>;**

### – similar to arrays, but…

- index operations disallowed: position\[i\] • read/write stream operators:

##### streamRead (positions, p\_ptr);

##### streamWrite (velocityfield, v\_ptr);

* * *

kernels

• functions applied to streams
– similar to for\_all construct

kernel void add (float a<>, float b<>,
out float result<>) {
for (i=0; i<100; i++)
result = a + b;
} c\[i\] = a\[i\]+b\[i\];

float a<100>;
float b<100>;
float c<100>;

add(a,b,c);

* * *

# Building GPU Computing Ecosystem

- Convince the world to program an entirely new kind of processor
- Tradeoffs between functional vs. performance requirements • Deliver HPC feature parity
- Seed larger ecosystem with foundational components

* * *

# CUDA: C on the GPU

- A simple, explicit programming language solution • Extend only where necessary **global** void KernelFunc(...); **shared** int SharedVar; KernelFunc<<< 500, 128 >>>(...); • Explicit GPU memory allocation — cudaMalloc(), cudaFree()
- Memory copy from host to device, etc. — cudaMemcpy(), cudaMemcpy2D(), ...

* * *

# CUDA: Threading in Data Parallel

- Threading in a data parallel world — Operations drive execution, not data
- Users simply given thread id — They decide what thread access which data element — One thread = single data element or block or variable or nothing…. — No need for accessors, views, or built-ins
- Flexibility — Not requiring the data layout to force the algorithm — Blocking computation for the memory hierarchy (shared)

### — Think about the algorithm, not the data

* * *

# Divergence in Parallel Computing

- Removing divergence pain from parallel programming
- SIMD Pain — User required to SIMD-ify — User suffers when computation goes divergent
- GPUs: Decouple execution width from programming model — Threads can diverge freely — Inefficiency only when granularity exceeds native machine width — Hardware managed — Managing divergence becomes performance optimization — Scalable

* * *

# Foundations

- Baseline HPC solution • Ubiquity: CUDA Everywhere
- Software — C99 Math.h — BLAS & FFT — GPU co-processor
- Hardware — IEEE math (G80) — Double Precision (GT200) — ECC (Fermi)

* * *

# Customizing Solutions

Ported Applications Domain Libraries Domain specific lang C Ease of Adoption Driver API PTX HW Generality

# Directions

- Hardware and Software are one • Within the Node

### — OS integration: Scheduling, Preemption, Virtual Memory — Results: Programming model simplification

- Expanding the cluster — Cluster wide communication and synchronization
- GPU on-load — Enhance the programming model to keep more of the computation

### (less cpu interaction) and more of the data (less host side shadowing).

Title: The Eras of GPU Development - ACM SIGGRAPH Blog
# The Eras of GPU Development

by [Jon Peddie](https://blog.siggraph.org/author/jonpeddie/ "Posts by Jon Peddie") \| 11 April 2025 \| [Hardware](https://blog.siggraph.org/category/hardware/)

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/SIGGRAPH-Blog-Header-New-9.png)

_Images and graphs provided by Jon Peddie_

## **Over 25 years, the versatile processor has touched almost every application.**

_As the GPU emerged, the number of processors within it expanded rapidly, surpassing the pace of Moore’s Law. This growth led to significant increases in compute density, enabling GPUs to handle not only computer graphics but also a broad range of computational tasks. The GPU has progressed through six distinct eras, with the latest advancements pushing it toward a more universal compute engine — an evolution that continues to unfold. Each era built upon the understanding and limitations of the previous one, progressing in a stepwise manner. These transitions were marked by the introduction of increasingly sophisticated APIs, primarily driven by Microsoft and closely followed by Khronos._

## **The Major GPU Eras**

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image.png)

Between the 1970s and 1999, graphics hardware was developed with specific applications in mind, including CAD, simulation, special effects, and gaming. The demand for greater processing power has always driven advancements in graphics technology. During this period, performance improvements outpaced transistor scaling, increasing at nearly 2.5 times per year — significantly exceeding the approximate 1.8 times annual growth predicted by transistor doubling. Figure 1. illustrates this trajectory, as documented by Professor John Poulton from the University of North Carolina. (UNC). [\[i\]](https://blog.siggraph.org/2025/04/evolution-of-gpus.html/#_edn1)

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image-1.png)

**_Figure 1. Performance of Graphics leading up to GPUs. Graphics hardware had been progressing at a rate faster than Moore’s law. (Data Courtesy of John Poulton, UNC Chapel Hill)_**

* * *

Using triangles per second as a metric, graphics hardware performance increased beyond what Moore’s Law predicted. This growth occurred because of the parallel nature of computer graphics computations, which hardware designers implemented effectively. PC graphics capabilities had advanced enough by 2001 that they made expensive specialized graphics systems unnecessary.

The development of GPUs corresponds with the introduction and evolution of DirectX, Microsoft’s graphics API that gained widespread adoption. DirectX became the framework that defined different GPU time periods because it standardized how hardware features were made available to software developers.

Hardware manufacturers initially created their own interfaces before Microsoft standardized the graphics landscape. These proprietary solutions gave developers access to specific features of graphics devices, yet resulted in fragmentation known as the “API wars.” This period created instability that posed risks to industry growth. Understanding GPU development requires examining how DirectX evolved and established new standards for graphics processing through its various iterations. The first era of the GPU began with the release of Microsoft’s DirectX 7.0, as shown in Figure 2.

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image-2.png)

**_Figure 2. The six eras of GPU evolution and development._**

* * *

**DirectX 7.0.** Microsoft released DirectX 7.0 in September 1999, marking a significant advancement in graphics processing capabilities. This version introduced hardware acceleration for transform and lighting operations alongside the ability to allocate vertex buffers directly in hardware memory. The implementation of hardware vertex buffers represented a notable improvement in Microsoft’s Direct3D technology, which was later renamed DirectX, giving it advantages over the competing OpenGL standard. DirectX 7.0 further enhanced rendering capabilities by incorporating multitexture hardware resources into its framework. During this period, DirectX 7.0 exemplified the pinnacle of fixed function multitexture pipeline capabilities, establishing new performance benchmarks before the industry’s eventual shift toward programmable shaders. (Figure 3)

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image-3.png)

**_Figure 3. DirectX basic pipeline._**

The most exciting features of DirectX 7 included hardware acceleration of transformation and lighting, cube environment mapping, vertex blending, and particle systems.

**DirectX 8.0**. Microsoft launched DirectX 8.0 in November 2000, introducing programmability through vertex and pixel shaders. This innovation freed developers from manually tracking hardware states, marking a fundamental shift in graphics programming.

**DirectX 8.1** arrived on 25 October 2001, targeting Windows 2000, XP, and derivative systems. This was followed by DirectX 8.1a in 2002, which updated the Direct3D component. June 2002 saw the release of DirectX 8.1b, addressing DirectShow issues on Windows 2000 systems. Microsoft also developed DirectX 8.2 specifically for DirectPlay functionality.

December 2002 brought **Direct3D 9**, enhancing the high-level shading language while supporting floating-point texture formats, multiple render targets, multiple-element textures, vertex shader texture lookups, and advanced stencil buffer techniques.

**DirectX 9.0c** emerged in August 2004, featuring Shader Model a3.0. This update expanded instruction capabilities for both vertex and pixel shaders, enabling developers to create substantially more sophisticated shader effects.

**Direct3D 10** arrived in November 2006, revolutionizing the traditional one-vertex-in/one-vertex-out model by allowing geometry generation entirely within GPU hardware. This version incorporated Shader Model 4.0, which extended vertex and pixel shader functionality while introducing the new geometry shader capability.

Microsoft released **DirectX 11** in October 2009 with Shader Model 5.0, which further expanded vertex, pixel, and geometry shader capabilities. This version introduced tessellation and compute shader profiles. Tessellation technology enabled runtime detail enhancement of wireframes using GPU rather than CPU resources.

Tessellation effectively transforms low-detail subdivision surfaces into higher-detail primitives directly on the GPU, breaking up high-order surfaces into structures optimized for rendering. This hardware implementation generated substantial visual detail, including displacement mapping support, without increasing model sizes or compromising refresh rates.

July 2015 saw the introduction of **DirectX 12**, providing lower-level hardware abstraction compared to previous versions. This approach improved multithreaded scaling and significantly reduced CPU utilization for games. DirectX 12 shared architectural elements with AMD’s Mantle API developed for consoles, similar to the Vulkan API.

DirectX 12 implemented Shader Model 5.1, adding volume-tiled resources, shader-specified stencils, improved collision and culling through conservative rasterization, rasterizer-ordered views, standard swizzles, default texture mapping, compressed resources, additional blend modes, and efficient order-independent transparency.

In November 2020, Microsoft introduced **DirectX 12 Ultimate**, bringing numerous new compute techniques and creating alignment between PC and game console development, substantially enhancing development efficiency. DirectX 12 Ultimate featured innovations such as Mesh Shaders and Sampler Feedback, with mesh shading particularly transforming image detail and quality without performance penalties.

A summary of the generations of DirectX is shown in Table 1.

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image-4.png)

**_Vs=vertex shader, gs=geometry shader, hs=hull shader, ps=pixel shader_**

**_Table 1. The evolution of the APIs and OS relative to the eras of GPUs._**

DirectX 12 extended the API to incorporate ray tracing and Direct12 Ultimate introduced mesh shaders and established the GPU platform as a computing device for graphics.

DirectX was the milestone of the eras of the GPU. Mesh shaders may not be the end of the trail. New designs are being experimented with using RISC-V which would create a new class of GPUs using MIMD architecture rather than the current and historical SIMD. Had Intel’s Larabee gone to market, it would have been the first MIMD GPU, but that’s a story for another time.

If you’re interested in GPUs and their history, take a look at the three volumes set of [“The History of the GPU”](https://link.springer.com/book/10.1007/978-3-031-10968-3).

![](https://blog.siggraph.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/image-6.png)
